=== ON-PREM P2.3 (distribution bundle) — branch redesign/onprem-p2.3-distribution-bundle ===
Base: origin/main. Plan: docs/superpowers/plans/2026-07-12-onprem-p2.3-distribution-bundle.md
Pre-flight finding: prior Phase 0 reviewer note deferred release checksums to "before P2.3" — added SHA256SUMS-only (owner declined signing) to the plan before dispatch (Task 6 + Task 5's INSTALL.md).
Task 1: complete (commits bb2d653..5104b2d, +2 fix waves cf20ed9 final). window.__ENV__ global + env.js.template + public/env.js + index.html + api.ts baseURL precedence. Review caught a real load-bearing gap: fonts.ts/impersonationSummary.ts computed their own 2-way URL fallback independently, which would've broken (silently fall to localhost:8008) in EVERY Docker deployment once Task 2 removes VITE_API_URL as a build arg — fixed by extracting shared getApiBaseUrl() into api.ts, all 3 call sites now use it. That fix itself caused a regression (ImpersonationBanner.test.tsx crashed entirely — misleading clean-looking pass summary while the whole suite silently failed to register — axios mock had no .create stub, caught by reviewer explicitly checking numFailedTestSuites via JSON reporter, not just the summary line) — fixed with a create() stub. Both fixes independently re-verified. 110/110 individual test assertions pass; the raw `vitest run` process still exits 1 because of uncaught errors, not test failures — noted, not fixed (pre-existing, already tracked separately as task_8e14f78f, unrelated to this branch): OrganizationDetail.test.tsx's IntersectionObserver jsdom gap throws outside any test body, failing the process gate despite every individual assertion passing.
Task 2: complete (commit cf20ed9..aff79b9, review clean/Approved). web/Dockerfile: envsubst-on-templates for env.js (NGINX_ENVSUBST_OUTPUT_DIR=/usr/share/nginx/html), VITE_API_URL build ARG/ENV removed. docker-compose.prod.yml: web's VITE_API_URL build-arg -> PUBLIC_API_URL runtime env var. NECESSARY DEVIATION from my own design spec's literal Dockerfile sample (a real bug in the spec, not just the implementer being cautious): /usr/share/nginx/html is pre-existing root-owned in the base image, and `COPY --chown` only sets ownership on entries it creates, NOT the pre-existing target directory — so the literal spec sample silently fails ("not writable", env.js never generated, feature doesn't work) under the unprivileged UID-101 runtime user. Fixed with USER root -> COPY --chown + explicit RUN chown -> USER nginx. Reviewer empirically reproduced the failure with the literal spec text, confirmed the fix works, confirmed non-root runtime preserved (docker exec id -> uid=101 nginx), and isolated that COPY --chown alone (without the RUN chown) is insufficient — all via real docker build/run, not just code reading. GOTCHA WORTH REMEMBERING for future nginx-unprivileged + envsubst-templates work: always explicitly chown any pre-existing base-image directory you're pointing NGINX_ENVSUBST_OUTPUT_DIR at.
Task 3: complete (commit aff79b9..a6bccb1, review clean/Approved). onprem/docker-compose.yml (published-image services, DEPLOYMENT_MODE hardcoded literal), onprem/.env.example (curated, on-prem-only vars), onprem/install.sh (preflight + idempotent secret generation). Both implementer and reviewer independently byte-diffed .env before/after a second install.sh run to prove true idempotency (not just trusting the printed message); confirmed BSD sed -i.bak behavior actually exercised on this machine, no stray .bak left; confirmed both missing-docker and missing-compose-v2 error paths exit 1 without creating .env. Diff against the brief's literal code is byte-identical, zero deviation.
Task 4: complete (commit a6bccb1..0e422b0, review clean/Approved). onprem/backup.sh + restore.sh, pg_dump/pg_restore wrappers via docker compose exec against the db service. Byte-identical to brief. Reviewer noted a soft design coupling (not a defect, inherent to the brief's own design): the scripts' own bash-level POSTGRES_USER/DB defaults are separate from what docker compose exec's .env-driven container actually uses — coincide in the common case but could diverge if .env sets non-default values without exporting them into the invoking shell. REMINDER FOR TASK 7: use non-default POSTGRES_USER/POSTGRES_DB in the live-verification .env to actually exercise this integration point, not just the defaults.
Task 5: complete (commit 0e422b0..db5435b, review clean/Approved). onprem/INSTALL.md — every concrete claim cross-checked by reviewer against Task 3/4's actual scripts/compose file (SHA256SUMS wording correctly frames it as a separate Releases-page download not bundled in the tarball, install.sh's advisory-not-blocking behavior matches doc, backup/restore invocation shapes match, /api/instance response shape verified against backend/main.go). Full teardown: docker compose down -v, all 5 scratch images removed, /tmp/onprem-verify removed.
UNRELATED PRE-EXISTING BUG FOUND (NOT fixed, out of scope, flagged separately via spawn_task task_17025c26): GetAttendees (backend/internal/handler/attendees.go:107-113) returns a nil Go slice as JSON `null` (not `[]`) when an event has zero attendees; the frontend's attendee-loading code does `.forEach()` on it with no null guard, crashing the entire event Manage page to a blank white screen for ANY event with zero attendees, in both SaaS and on-prem. Confirmed via `git diff origin/main -- backend/internal/handler/attendees.go` that this branch made zero changes to that file -- fully pre-existing on main, unrelated to P2.3. Worked around for verification by seeding one attendee directly via the API before opening the Manage page.
ALL 7 TASKS COMPLETE (6 implementation + 1 live verification, with 1 real bug found and fixed during verification itself). NEXT: final whole-branch review (opus), covering commits through the backup.sh/restore.sh .env-sourcing fix.
Final whole-branch review (opus): Ready to merge YES, 0 Critical. 1 Important finding, fixed: backup.sh/restore.sh's `source .env` (commit 44b1ca5) is more fragile than docker compose's own .env parser -- bash `source` chokes on values compose accepts unquoted, e.g. .env.example's own documented `IDENTO_ORG_NAME=My Organization` (space) or a comma-separated CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGINS with a space after the comma, aborting the script (exit 127, "command not found") before pg_dump/pg_restore ever runs. Fixed in commit d61c923 by reading POSTGRES_USER/POSTGRES_DB directly from the running db container (`docker compose exec -T db printenv <VAR>`) instead of re-parsing .env at all -- the container already has the correct compose-resolved values regardless of quoting style. Controller live-verified the fix against the exact failure scenario (spaced IDENTO_ORG_NAME + comma-space CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGINS in .env): backup succeeded. Verification also caught a SECOND real bug introduced by the printenv approach itself before it was ever committed: two `docker compose exec -T` calls sharing the script's stdin with restore.sh's own interactive "Type 'restore' to confirm" prompt starved the read (exec -T forwards/consumes stdin even for a command like printenv that doesn't need input) -- confirmation silently failed via `set -e` on read's EOF, never reaching "Aborted." Fixed by redirecting both printenv calls from /dev/null. Re-verified live: backup + restore (with the spaced/comma .env AND with the confirmation prompt via a real held-open stdin, not a one-shot pipe) both succeeded correctly. 3 Minor findings from the review: (1) install.sh didn't preflight for `openssl` presence -- fixed in the CodeRabbit-review fix wave below; (2) env.js had no explicit no-store Cache-Control header -- fixed in the same wave; (3) informational only, not a defect -- any out-of-repo SaaS deploy pipeline still passing the now-removed VITE_API_URL build-arg would be silently ignored (by design, confirmed intentional scope). No regressions to SaaS-mode behavior found (window.__ENV__ defaults to {} so api.ts/fonts.ts/impersonationSummary.ts fall through to VITE_API_URL exactly as before this branch).

CODERABBIT PR REVIEW ROUND (PR #43): 14 actionable inline comments. Verified each against current code (several targeted the historical plan doc, describing gaps already closed in real code during implementation -- those were left as-is, plan docs are point-in-time records, not living code). Fixed 7 real, still-live issues: (1) `.github/workflows/release.yml`'s onprem-bundle step interpolated `github.ref_name` directly into a shell command (zizmor: template-injection) -- now passed via `env:` + validated against `[A-Za-z0-9._-]` before use; (2) `web/src/lib/__tests__/api.test.ts`'s fallback tests never stubbed `VITE_API_URL`, so a real `.env`/CI-set value could flip them to pass/fail for the wrong reason -- added `vi.stubEnv`/`vi.unstubAllEnvs`, plus the missing middle-tier "falls back to VITE_API_URL" test (5 tests now, was 4); (3) `web/nginx.conf` had no cache header for `/env.js` (regenerated at every container start) -- added `location = /env.js { add_header Cache-Control "no-store"; }`; (4) `onprem/install.sh` didn't preflight `openssl` -- a missing-openssl host would create `.env` with placeholder `change-me` secrets and then the idempotency guard would lock them in on every retry -- added an openssl check alongside the existing docker/compose checks, before `.env` is created; (5) `onprem/install.sh` left the generated `.env` (containing JWT_SECRET/POSTGRES_PASSWORD) at the default `cp` umask -- added `chmod 600 .env`; (6) `onprem/restore.sh`'s `pg_restore --clean --if-exists` ran against a live backend, risking DROP failures from active connections or the backend reading a partially-restored database -- now stops `backend` before restoring and restarts it after, with `INSTALL.md` updated to document the brief outage; (7) `.superpowers/sdd/progress.md` itself had two accuracy gaps CodeRabbit caught -- Task 1's "110/110 tests pass" didn't distinguish passing assertions from vitest's own exit-1 process status (pre-existing IntersectionObserver gap, unrelated), and the final-review entry had a literal `<pending>` commit placeholder never backfilled with the real hash (d61c923) -- both corrected above. Deliberately NOT fixed, with reasons: (a) "gate image publication on CI success" (Major, tagged 🏗️ Heavy lift by the tool itself) -- real gap, but pre-existing on `backend-image` (unchanged by this PR, shipped in an earlier PR) and would require restructuring the whole release pipeline's trigger model (ci.yml runs on push/PR, not tag push) to fix properly for both jobs consistently; flagged separately as a follow-up rather than done piecemeal inside this PR. (b) GitGuardian's 2 "hardcoded secret" findings on `onprem/docker-compose.yml` lines 7/26 -- confirmed false positives on inspection: those lines are Compose's `${VAR:?error message}` required-variable syntax (`POSTGRES_PASSWORD`/`IDENTO_ADMIN_PASSWORD`), no actual secret value present, GitGuardian's heuristic misfired on the variable name + message text. (c) plan-doc-only findings (Task 1 file list, nginx chown sequence, backup/restore .env-sourcing) -- all already fixed in the real, current code during implementation or the earlier fix waves above; editing historical plan text to match wasn't judged worth the diff noise. Backend 176/176, frontend 111/111 (was 110, +1 new middle-tier test in api.test.ts) both green after this wave. ALL WORK COMPLETE, ready for finishing-a-development-branch.

=== ON-PREM P2.4 (client compatibility pass) — branch redesign/onprem-p2.4-client-compatibility ===

Step 1 (iOS compile): `:shared:compileKotlinIosSimulatorArm64 :shared:compileKotlinIosArm64 :shared:compileTestKotlinIosSimulatorArm64 :shared:iosSimulatorArm64Test` — BUILD SUCCESSFUL, all commonTest sources (incl. Task 1/3's new tests) pass under Kotlin/Native, not just the JVM run each task already did.
Step 2-4 (Server URL screen, live apply, persistence): reached the Server URL screen via "Advanced: change server" on first launch, entered `http://10.0.2.2:18008` (emulator's host-loopback alias for the on-prem stack), tapped Test connection — reported `Connected (onprem)`. Saved; the very next network request (into the setup wizard) reached the on-prem server with no restart. Force-quit and relaunched the app — URL was still in effect (DataStore persistence survived a cold start, not just the in-memory cache; independently re-confirmed a second time after a full app reinstall in Step 9's retest, where the same URL was still present).
Step 5-6 (setup wizard + Registration check-in): created a manager user directly via API (worked around the pre-existing admin-role provisioning-token rejection, same gap flagged in `task_56790857`), completed the QR-provisioning wizard's manager-login fallback path (Event -> Registration mode -> DayZone -> Printer -> Complete), reached the Registration home screen. Created a test attendee via API (code ANDROID-001). Search tab returned "No results" for "Android"/"ANDROID-001" — investigated via backend logs (`docker compose logs backend`) instead of assuming: found a genuine SQL syntax error (`ERROR: syntax error at or near "ESCAPE"`, SQLSTATE 42601) in `GetAttendeesByEventID`'s search filter, 100% reproducible on every non-empty search. Root cause: `pg_store.go` attached one `ESCAPE '\\'` clause after a parenthesized 4-way `OR` of `ILIKE` predicates instead of one per predicate — invalid Postgres syntax. Invisible to the existing test suite because it's pgxmock-based (regex-matches query text, never executes against real Postgres). FIXED on a separate branch `fix/attendee-search-escape-syntax` (PR #51, commit 78fb67c): ESCAPE moved to each ILIKE predicate individually; updated the one pgxmock regex assertion that depended on the old (broken) query text; additionally verified against the real on-prem Postgres by rebuilding the backend image and re-running the search — confirmed correct (name/code search both matched, an escaped-wildcard search correctly matched nothing). Re-tested from the mobile app after redeploying the fixed image: search for "Android" now found "Android Tester", tapping the result triggered an immediate check-in ("PASSED", CHECKED IN counter incremented 0->1), confirmed server-side via GET /api/events/:id/attendees (checkin_status:true, checked_in_by/checked_in_device_number/checked_in_point_name all correctly populated).
Step 7 (badge printing through the print agent): ran the real `agent/` Go binary in `--mock` mode (3 mock printers, no physical hardware needed) with `AGENT_ALLOWED_ORIGINS` set per Task 7's new INSTALL.md guidance. Verified the agent's CORS+auth behavior directly: `/health`/`/printers`/`/print` all succeed with an allowed Origin + loopback Host + JSON content-type (with or without the bearer token — both auth paths work as designed); `/print` correctly returns 401 for a disallowed Origin or no Origin at all without a token. Ran the desktop "Idento Kiosk" app via its Vite dev server (`npm run dev`, added as `.claude/launch.json`'s `desktop-p24verify` entry) in the Browser preview pane — no code changes needed, confirming the design spec's assumption. Logged in against the on-prem backend (had to add the dev server's origin to the test `.env`'s `CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGINS`, a limitation of this ad-hoc test setup, not a real bug), listed the "P24 Verify Event", opened Equipment Settings — it auto-connected to the mock agent (3 printers), set Zebra_ZD420_Mock as default (confirmed via `POST /printers/default` -> 200 + UI star + toast). Could not trigger a live scan-to-print through the check-in UI itself (it polls the agent's `/scan/last`, which only reflects real scanner hardware — no mock-injection endpoint exists in the agent's API surface, and keyboard-wedge input isn't wired to any listener here). Instead exercised the exact same code path `printBadge()` uses, end-to-end via curl: fetched real ZPL from the on-prem backend's `POST /api/events/:id/badge-zpl` for the checked-in ANDROID-001 attendee (200, real ZPL returned), then POSTed that ZPL to the local agent's `/print` exactly as the desktop app's `printBadge()` does (200, `{"status":"printed"}`). This proves the full chain — on-prem badge generation -> local agent delivery -> configured printer — without needing physical hardware; only the final physical print output itself wasn't observable (no printer attached to this environment, an honest, expected limitation, not a defect).
Step 8 (HTTP/private-host validation gate): in the Server URL screen, entered `http://8.8.8.8` (public IP) -> tapped Save -> correctly rejected inline with "Plain http:// is only allowed for local network addresses. Use https:// for a public server." (field outlined red). Changed to `https://8.8.8.8` -> field immediately turned green, error cleared, Save allowed. Tapped Test Connection -> request correctly went out (reached `https://dns.google/api/instance`, since 8.8.8.8:443 is Google's real DoH endpoint) and correctly reported a connection failure (404 + a NoTransformationFoundException-shaped message) — exactly the plan's anticipated outcome ("even if the connection test against it fails... the point is the validation gate itself"). Validation gate behavior confirmed correct on both sides.
Step 9 (suspended-tenant handling — REAL BUG FOUND AND FIXED): suspended the on-prem tenant directly via `UPDATE tenants SET status='suspended'` (no super-admin UI path exists or is meant to exist for a single-tenant on-prem install; this exercises the same backend 403 a SaaS suspension would). Attempted to sign in as the bootstrap admin — login itself succeeded (AuthApiService already checks response status correctly), but the very next call (`GetEvents`, "Choose an event" screen) crashed with a raw kotlinx.serialization exception: `Illegal input: Unexpected JSON token at offset 0: Expected start of the array '[', but had '{' instead`. Root cause: the backend correctly returns `{"code":"tenant_suspended","error":"This organization is suspended. Contact support."}` on 403, but `EventApiService.getEvents()` (and every sibling method across EventApiService/AttendeeApiService/StationApiService/ZoneApiService) called bare `.body()` without checking `response.status` first, so Ktor tried to deserialize the error object directly as `List<Event>`. This is exactly the client-side half of the error-handling defect already flagged in `task_56790857` (mobile station-provisioning), confirmed to be the same systemic pattern across the whole API layer, not a one-off. FIXED on a separate branch `fix/api-error-body-surfacing` (PR #55, commit 982fef4): added an opt-in `bodyOrApiError()` extension (throws `ApiErrorException` with the backend's real `error` message on non-2xx, parsed via a standalone unit-tested `parseApiErrorBody()`), applied at all ~15 vulnerable call sites across the 4 services; deliberately did NOT add a global `HttpResponseValidator` since that would have changed behavior on AuthApiService's and AttendeeApiService.checkinAttendee's already-correct manual status-check paths. 4 new unit tests (pure JSON-parsing logic, no HTTP client, matching this codebase's established precedent for the network layer). Re-verified live: rebuilt the release APK with the fix applied (as a scratch/uncommitted copy in this worktree, since P2.4's own build.gradle.kts already provides the signing config needed), reinstalled fresh, repeated the exact suspend-and-login sequence — the app now shows "This organization is suspended. Contact support." (the backend's real message) instead of the crash. Reactivated the tenant afterward, confirmed events list loads normally again.
Step 10 (teardown): all 3 spawned agent processes killed (mock print agent instances on ports 3737 and 12345), `docker compose down -v` (containers + volume + network removed), scratch backend/web images removed (`ghcr.io/thevladbog/idento-backend:p24verify`, `:idento-web:p24verify`), `/tmp/onprem-p24-verify` removed, release APK uninstalled from the emulator, desktop Vite dev server stopped. The 3 scratch/local-only files applied to this worktree during verification (androidApp/build.gradle.kts's temporary signing config, AppModule.android.kt's Koin-cycle-fix copy, the 5 API-error-fix files' copy, web/src/test/setup.ts's IntersectionObserver-fix copy) were all reverted via `git checkout --` before this entry was written — confirmed via `git status --short` showing only this progress.md file modified. The real fixes live on their own PRs: #49 (IntersectionObserver), #50 (Koin circular dependency), #51 (attendee search ESCAPE syntax), #55 (API error body surfacing) — none of them are part of this branch's diff.
ALL 8 TASKS COMPLETE. 3 real, severe, pre-existing bugs found during live verification and fixed on dedicated branches (not this one): PR #50 (100%-reproducible app-launch crash via Koin circular dependency), PR #51 (100%-reproducible attendee-search SQL syntax error), PR #55 (API error responses crashing instead of displaying, confirmed systemic across 4 services). Plus PR #49 (pre-existing release-pipeline-breaking TypeScript error, found while building the web image for this verification). NEXT: final whole-branch review (opus), then finishing-a-development-branch.

CRITICAL FINDING (verified empirically, not just by reading): UploadEventFont (POST /api/events/{event_id}/fonts) has a real, currently-shipping bug — after requireEventOwnership correctly reads *models.JWTCustomClaims from context, the handler re-extracts the caller's identity a SECOND time via `c.Get("user").(*jwt.Token)`, a type middleware.JWT() never stores there (it stores *models.JWTCustomClaims). That assertion can never succeed once ownership already passed, so the handler unconditionally 401s right after every ownership check — the license-acceptance check, field validation, file parsing, and Store.CreateFont are all dead code today. Proven via TestContractUploadEventFont: a fully well-formed multipart upload (valid ownership, license_accepted=true, name/family/file all present) still returns 401, never 201. Documented precisely in openapi.yaml (401 as the practical contract; 201/409/500-save marked UNREACHABLE with the mechanism explained) rather than silently "fixed" — out of this task's scope per P0.3 rule (spec must match code, not vice versa). Flagged via spawn_task for a follow-up fix session (font upload is business-critical per the parent design spec). Other findings: GET /api/fonts/{id}/file's route-registration comment says "Public font file endpoint" but it's actually registered on the JWT-protected `api` group (api.Use(middleware.JWT()) applies before this route is added) — documented as protected, comment is stale; DeleteEventFont's cross-event mismatch uses 403 (not the usual 404-masking pattern) since Store.GetFontByID looks up by ID alone; text/css and font/* (wildcard covering woff2/woff/ttf/otf) responses both needed `format: binary` in the harness even though CSS is genuinely UTF-8 text, because openapi3filter has no registered body decoder for either media type and only routes through the safe raw-bytes fallback when the schema says binary (same technique already used for image/png). GetEventFonts's nil-slice-becomes-[] guard tested directly (Store.GetFontsByEventID's real impl can return nil for zero rows; GetAPIKeys needed no such guard since its real impl always initializes []). DEVIATION FROM BRIEF, flagged for review: ATTENDEES_LIST_KEY(eventId) does NOT return the brief's literal 2-element `["get", "/api/events/{event_id}/attendees"]` -- that literal, kept exactly, leaves the `eventId` parameter completely unused, which fails this repo's tsconfig (noUnusedParameters: true) and eslint (no-unused-vars) rather than just being unidiomatic. Implemented instead as `["get", "/api/events/{event_id}/attendees", { params: { path: { event_id: eventId } } }]` -- still a genuine TanStack prefix match (query.page/per_page/search/zone/status live under params.query, which isn't in the filter key, so partialMatchKey ignores them and every page/filter variant for that event still matches), but now correctly scoped to one event instead of every event sharing this route template. Verified two ways: (1) read node_modules/openapi-react-query/src/index.ts -- queryKey = init===undefined ? [method,path] : [method,path,init], path is the raw unsubstituted OpenAPI template, init nests {params:{path:{event_id},query:{...}}}; and node_modules/@tanstack/query-core's partialMatchKey(actualKey, filterKey) = Object.keys(filterKey).every(k => partialMatchKey(actualKey[k], filterKey[k])), recursing into plain objects the same way, confirming a filter key ending in {params:{path:{event_id}}} (no `query` sub-key) matches any actual key regardless of its query contents. (2) hooks.test.tsx's "ATTENDEES_LIST_KEY" describe block: two same-event queries with different page/search params both refetch after invalidateQueries({queryKey: ATTENDEES_LIST_KEY(eventId)}); a third query for a *different* eventId does not refetch, proving the scoping is real, not accidental. 7 new tests (MSW request-capture for param presence/absence including the empty-string-search edge case, envelope-shape assertion, 2x invalidation-prefix, zones fetch) + full 194/194 suite, typecheck/eslint clean.

Task 6: complete (commit 30fb991, pending review). BulkBar mounted above AttendeeTable in AttendeesPage whenever selectedAttendees (derived by filtering current-page `rows` against the existing `selected: Set<string>`, not a new piece of state) is non-empty -- deliberate consequence: a bulk delete's invalidate+refetch naturally drops deleted rows out of `rows`, so the bar disappears on its own without BulkBar needing to call onClear itself. Assign zone and Delete both loop sequentially (not Promise.all) over `selected`, calling the shared $api mutation's mutateAsync per id with a live {done,total} progress readout; both use an incrementing session-id ref (ApiKeysCard/DangerZoneCard pattern) bumped on every explicit dialog close -- the loop checks the ref before each iteration (stops issuing further requests once cancelled) and before each progress-state update (stops a late/cancelled-session response from resurfacing stale UI), while list invalidation itself runs unconditionally whenever at least one request in the batch was actually attempted (cache correctness independent of cancellation). Assign-zone dialog deliberately does NOT auto-close on completion -- it shows the final "x / x" readout and waits for an explicit close; this also sidesteps a real test race (auto-closing immediately after the last progress tick made the "x/y" text unobservable in a fast MSW test run). Delete DOES auto-close on full success (matches DangerZoneCard) but stays open with an inline i18n'd error (bulkDeleteError) on any individual failure, never force-closing/discarding the typed count. CSV export (exportCsv.ts): sanitizeCsvField mirrors the backend's formula-injection guard verbatim -- values starting with =,+,-,@,tab,or CR get a leading apostrophe BEFORE standard CSV quoting is applied (order matters: a prefixed "-1,2" becomes "'-1,2" then gets quoted because of the comma, not before); UTF-8 BOM prepended for Excel/Cyrillic; columns = 6 fixed fields + checked_in(yes/no, real field not fabricated) + union of custom_fields keys across selected rows (first-seen order, missing key -> empty cell, never invented). CSV column headers are plain English literals, NOT i18n keys -- deliberate call, since the brief's exhaustive bulkXxx i18n key list has no CSV-header keys and a CSV is a data-interchange format for Excel/re-import tooling, not app chrome. Blob verification in jsdom: confirmed directly that jsdom's Blob has no .text()/.arrayBuffer() (both undefined on the prototype) unlike Node's native Blob, so exportCsv.test.ts reads the downloaded Blob via FileReader.readAsArrayBuffer + TextDecoder("utf-8",{ignoreBOM:true}) -- readAsText alone silently strips the leading BOM (spec'd decoder behavior, verified separately), which would make a "starts with the BOM" assertion pass vacuously; ignoreBOM:true keeps the literal U+FEFF character so the test exercises what actually got downloaded. Print badges chip is a plain <span> (not <button>, no onClick), asserted via tagName + queryByRole('button') absence. 236/236 panel tests (12 new exportCsv, 11 new BulkBar, 1 new AttendeesPage bar-appears/disappears), typecheck+eslint clean.

=== PANEL P2.1 — POST-MERGE CODERABBIT FIX ROUND (PR #65) — reconciled after a real concurrent-write incident, HEAD=53fe462 ===
User pasted CodeRabbit's full review-comment dump on PR #65 (14 Inline Critical/Major findings across backend Go and frontend TS) with the instruction: verify each against current code, fix only still-valid issues, keep changes minimal, validate. Backend findings (users.go admin/manager role check on UnassignStaffFromEvent, pg_store.go error wrapping + pagination overflow guard, openapi.yaml BulkImportResponse.errors required, create_failed contract-test coverage) were dispatched to one subagent and landed cleanly: commits 7b0fb74/9b9d8ea/fde41ae/6447e79/175c44d, all green.
INCIDENT: the frontend findings were split across 4 PARALLEL subagents dispatched into the SAME unisolated working directory (no isolation:"worktree"), each expected to commit its own fixes. Because subagents perform git commits concurrently against one shared checkout, one agent's stale-tree commit (19dcac1, ostensibly "AttendeeTable keyboard-accessible") accidentally REVERTED two other agents' already-completed, real fixes: EditAttendeeForm.tsx/AttendeeDrawer.test.tsx's PATCH trim-vs-baseline fix (24a1b5a) and parseCsv.ts/parseCsv.test.ts's PapaParse-errors fix (6a2342e). Root cause: parallel subagents + git writes + shared working tree = races that can silently un-do completed, verified work with no error surfaced anywhere.
RECOVERY (methodology, not just outcome): stopped both still-running agents immediately via TaskStop; safety-snapshotted the ENTIRE working tree via `git stash push -u` before touching anything further; verified each previously-claimed-fixed file definitively via `git diff <source-commit>:<path> HEAD:<path>` (empty diff = correctly intact, non-empty = actually reverted) rather than trusting any subagent's self-report -- this caught that EditAttendeeForm.tsx/AttendeeDrawer.test.tsx had ALREADY been correctly restored by Agent 2's own fixup commit (5b98961), but parseCsv.ts/parseCsv.test.ts were STILL reverted, requiring a manual `git checkout 6a2342e -- <paths>` restore (commit 6c824e6), verified byte-identical via diff before committing. Then reconciled the remaining interrupted agents' work file-by-file: completed wizardState.ts's Fix 4 (dedupeByEmail/buildBulkPayload originalIndices/originalRowIndices threading -- the ImportWizard-group agent had fully written the CONSUMER side in ImportWizard.tsx before being killed, but never reached the PRODUCER side in wizardState.ts; the consumer's already-written, well-commented code served as an unambiguous spec for the missing piece, implemented directly rather than via another subagent dispatch to avoid repeating the parallel-write risk) plus 4 new dedicated unit tests for the new return fields; verified AttendeeDrawer.tsx/EditAttendeeForm.tsx's Fix 2 (busy-state bridged from EditAttendeeForm to AttendeeDrawer's outer Sheet via onBusyChange/isEditBusyRef, blocking Escape/outside-click mid-save) and Fix 3 (explicit zoneAccessLoading||zonesLoading gate on the +Zone affordance) by reading the actual source and cross-checking against passing targeted tests; verified BulkBar.tsx/AttendeesPage.tsx's Fix 3-6 (assign-dialog busy-gating, honest partial-failure readout via assignFailedCount, Button-primitive swap for 5 raw <button> elements) the same way; verified ImportWizard.tsx's Fix 1/2/3 UI wiring (validateMapping gating the Import button, isStep1Busy gating DialogContent's dismiss handlers, step1ParseError blocking the step 1->2 transition) by reading the full 1120-line file and confirming every fix's wiring end-to-end, not just its existence. Also discovered and independently reconciled a THIRD, older stash (Agent 2's own pre-incident auto-recovery snapshot, stash@{1}, based on commit 175c44d) -- diffed it file-by-file against the post-reconciliation HEAD and confirmed every file it touched was either already superseded (AttendeeTable.test.tsx -- HEAD has strictly more coverage), functionally identical modulo comment wording (wizardState.ts), or already committed pre-incident (AddAttendeeDialog.tsx/test.tsx, via a78f25b) -- so nothing further was recoverable from it; left both spent stashes (stash@{0}, stash@{1}) in place rather than dropping them, per the standing git-safety practice of not running destructive operations without explicit instruction.
Committed in 4 logically-scoped groups matching the fix groupings: e711991 (ImportWizard Fix 1/2/3/4 + wizardState.ts/test.ts), deb4e68 (AttendeeDrawer/EditAttendeeForm Fix 2/3), 8d5f5f6 (BulkBar/AttendeesPage Fix 3-6), 53fe462 (the 4 i18n keys those groups needed, added as a small follow-up since the earlier commits referenced keys not yet present in en.json/ru.json -- a minor historical inconsistency in isolated commits, harmless in the final squashed/merged state since the branch is reviewed as a whole).
Full verification sweep after reconciliation: 371/371 panel tests (up from 366 pre-incident -- 5 new wizardState.ts tests), panel typecheck clean, `npx eslint .` clean, 304/304 backend tests (OPENAPI_COVERAGE=1), golangci-lint clean. Pushed to origin (15 commits ahead). All 14 CodeRabbit review threads on PR #65 replied to (each citing its specific landed commit) and resolved via GraphQL addPullRequestReviewThreadReply + resolveReviewThread.
LESSON (captured to memory as feedback, see panel-rewrite-status.md): never dispatch multiple PARALLEL subagents into the SAME unisolated working directory when any of them perform git commits -- use isolation:"worktree" per agent, or dispatch sequentially, whenever concurrent writers could touch the same checkout. The Agent tool's worktree isolation exists specifically to prevent this class of failure.

=== PANEL P2.1 — CODEX REVIEW FIX ROUND (PR #65) — HEAD=95010f6 ===
User asked to fetch and address new PR #65 review comments. CodeRabbit's own re-review was rate-limited (org review-limit hit), but a Codex review (chatgpt-codex-connector, triggered via an existing "@codex review" comment on the PR) had already posted 9 new inline findings (1 P1, 7 P2, 1 P3) across backend and frontend files not touched by the earlier CodeRabbit round. Verified each against current code before fixing (same discipline as the CodeRabbit round) -- all 9 confirmed real, none dismissed.
Most serious: UpdateAttendee's SQL UPDATE statement never included the `code` column in its SET clause (backend/internal/store/pg_store.go) -- AttendeeDrawer's "Regenerate code" feature set attendee.Code in memory and the handler reported success, but the write silently never reached Postgres. Every existing test stubs the store (fakeStore/pgxmock echoing back whatever it's told), so nothing caught this until a NEW pgxmock test asserted the actual SQL text (`code = ` present, bound value in exec args) -- another instance of the "ZERO real-Postgres test infrastructure" gap already on record from P2.1's own retro. Fixed + tested, commit d3d7119.
Second most serious (P1, frontend): ImportWizard's step-3 isStep3Busy treated a persistent chunkFailure as permanently "busy" -- a chunk POST rejecting with an error that can never succeed on retry (e.g. the backend's attendees_per_event limit) left the dialog with no ✕, blocked Escape/outside-click, AND (the footer's own render condition being `!isImporting && !chunkFailure`) literally no footer at all, trapping the operator until a page reload. Fixed by dropping chunkFailure from isStep3Busy and changing the footer's render condition to `!isImporting`, so a SETTLED failure (nothing actively in flight) is dismissable via Done while "Retry remaining" stays available. This flipped an existing test's assertion ("no Done while a retry is pending") which was itself pinning the bug -- updated to assert Done IS present once settled, matching the new correct behavior. Commit 71e4ae7.
Remaining 7, all confirmed and fixed: wizardState.ts's validateMapping missed a custom field name colliding CASE-INSENSITIVELY with a standard field (backend lowercases keys before matching its own standardFields set -- e.g. custom "Email" silently overwrites the real email field); AttendeeDrawer's zone add/remove only invalidated the zone-access query, leaving a zone-filtered attendees table stale (now also invalidates ATTENDEES_LIST_KEY, both directions); addZoneAccess had no onError handling (now shows an inline error, new key drawerAddZoneError); AttendeeTable's trailing ellipsis was an independently-focusable button whose aria-label falsely advertised a working row menu -- keyboard/screen-reader activation landed on the drawer instead (now tabIndex={-1}+aria-hidden, pure decoration, mouse click still bubbles to the row unchanged); ImportWizard's encoding-change reparse had no ordering guard within one open session -- a rapid double-click could let an earlier slower parse overwrite a later faster one's result (fixed primarily by disabling both encoding segments for the reparse's duration, which closes the race at the only UI entry point; a per-call token guard added as defense-in-depth for future non-UI callers); exportCsv.ts's customFieldKeys included standard field names duplicated in custom_fields (bulk_import.go stores EVERY incoming key there, including ones it also mapped to a standard column) -- now filtered case-insensitively; attendees search placeholder said "Search name, company, code…" but the backend only ever searched first/last name, email, code (never company) -- corrected the copy in both locales rather than expanding backend search scope unasked.
All fixes committed in 6 scoped commits (27b3840 wizardState collision, 71e4ae7 ImportWizard dismiss+race, 916d074 AttendeeDrawer zone invalidation+error+search-copy i18n, 7f3171d AttendeeTable ellipsis, 95010f6 exportCsv+search-copy test), each with its own new/updated test coverage. Full sweep: 380/380 panel tests (up from 371), panel typecheck/eslint clean, 305/305 backend tests, golangci-lint clean. Pushed. All 9 Codex review threads replied to (each citing its landed commit) and resolved via GraphQL.

=== P3.2 FOLLOW-UP — raster align/valign fix (found during the printed-matrix Zebra exit gate) ===
The physical run surfaced a real defect in reconciliation #7's raster branch: EN names printed centered (native ^FB path) but RU names printed left-pinned (raster path drops align entirely) — same template, same `align: "center"`. TDD fix: `RasterResult` gains `width`/`height` (the rasterized bitmap's own measured dot size, never emitted in ^GFA bytes — `zplImage.ts`'s `bitmapToZPLHex`); new pure `rasterFieldOrigin(element, dpi, raster)` in `generateZpl.ts` computes an `^FO` offset from align/valign the same way the native branch's ^FB justification/valign-y-shift do (center=half slack, right/bottom=full slack, gated on width/height presence, negative slack clamped to 0 so an oversized raster never drifts backward past the element's own x/y). Wired into `generateTextZPL`'s raster branch AND `ZplPreviewModal.tsx`'s Rendered-tab raster-text draw (same helper, so preview can't drift from print). rotation and ^FB-wrap/maxLines remain dropped on this branch (still-documented, unchanged). New goldens: 2 generateZpl.test.ts raster-branch cases rewritten (offset math spelled out) + 2 new (overflow-clamp, width/height-unset no-op) + 7 new rasterFieldOrigin unit tests; goldenMatrix.test.ts mock rasterizer extended with width/height (matrix fixture sets no align/valign on text elements, so its existing goldens were unaffected by design — verified, not assumed). zplImage.test.ts's 4 bitmapToZPLHex/buildGfaCommand assertions updated for the new fields. Docs: plan doc `docs/superpowers/plans/2026-07-16-panel-p3.2-print-truth.md` reconciliation #7 gets a dated addendum (deviation half-lifted) + Task 1 Produces line updated; `panel/AGENTS.md` has no raster-specific comment to update (checked, none exists — only the file-list exception class, unaffected). Gates: 334/334 badge-feature tests + 1397/1397 full panel suite, typecheck clean, eslint clean, build succeeds (pre-existing >500kB chunk warning only).

EMPIRICALLY VERIFIED (not just reasoned): destroyed the local db volume + container, recreated genuinely empty (0 tables), hit a real second-order snag mid-verification (a stray compiled backend binary -- `go run`'s child process, not matched by `pgrep -f "go run main.go"` -- was still bound to :8008 from an earlier task and answering curl checks against a since-destroyed database, producing a misleading "Database error" on login; killed by PID once found), then re-ran clean: backend started fresh, applied all 25 migrations, bootstrap created admin@test.com/password successfully (log: "bootstrap: created organization \"My Organization\" with admin admin@test.com"), login returned a real 200+token, and the FULL Playwright suite passed (1 passed, 9.5s) against that from-scratch-bootstrapped backend -- the exact sequence CI now runs. Direct npx eslint clean, typecheck+build clean. FINDING (inherited verbatim from the plan's own brief, not an implementer deviation): reconnectAgent()/switchAgentMode() have no sequence/cancellation guard against the pre-existing mount effect or against overlapping calls -- e.g. toggling to External with a bad URL while the initial health-check is still in flight could let whichever async chain settles last silently overwrite agentConnected/printer state with stale data. Confined to a manual pre-flight config screen (not the live run screen), no server writes involved (pure local UI state), self-correcting via reload or re-toggle -- judged Minor/deferred rather than a blocking data-safety issue (unlike K2a's Task 12 settings-save race, which risked a real server-side overwrite). Flagged for the final whole-branch review to decide whether a sequence-token guard is worth adding.

Module namespace is not configurable in ESM" against the real installed ESM package (unlike Vite-transformed in-project modules) -- fixed by reusing Task 5's already-established vi.mock("@tauri-apps/api/core", ...) pattern in the same file; reviewer confirmed the mock is file-scoped and doesn't leak into sibling tests (full suite including useAgentSupervisor.test.tsx itself still 69/69).

IMPORTANT FOUND+FIXED (real bug in the plan's own script text, not implementer deviation -- judged an unambiguous shell-scripting bug, fixed directly like K2a's plan-bug precedents): under set -euo pipefail, HOST_IP="$(hostname -I ... | awk ...)" and the token-retry loop's TOKEN="$(grep ... | sed ...)" both abort the ENTIRE script if their left-hand command fails (realistic on a freshly-imaged Pi with no network yet) -- for HOST_IP, right after the systemd service was already installed/started but BEFORE ever printing the Base URL/Token block the operator needs. Fixed with `|| true` appended inside each pipeline (2-line fix, commit 966bc5a). One justified deviation from the brief's literal test-file source: explicit `import { describe, it, expect } from "vitest"` added (reviewer verified ALL 24 existing web/ test files already use this convention despite `globals: true`, and it's required for `tsc -b` to typecheck the file). Gates: web 24 files/357 tests, build clean, lint clean.
Task 2: complete (commit a6cbbec, controller-run final regression sweep + ledger, verify-only, no functional changes). Full gate re-run from scratch rather than trusting Task 1's own report: `cd web && npm run test` -> 24 files/357 tests, all green (includes i18n-key-usage.test.ts's 261 call-site assertions); `npm run lint` -> 0 issues; `npm run build` (`tsc -b && vite build`) -> clean, only the pre-existing >500kB single-chunk advisory (unrelated to this branch, no code-splitting was ever in scope here). The new regression test (`i18n-key-usage.test.ts`) statically walks every `.ts`/`.tsx` under `web/src`, extracts literal `t("key")` call-site strings via regex, and asserts each resolves in both the `en` and `ru` resource trees — it catches any future literal call site referencing a key absent from either language, but deliberately does NOT (and structurally cannot) catch dynamically-constructed keys (e.g. `` t(`tenantStatus_${status}`) ``), which the spec explicitly scoped out as a separate, riskier problem. Per the spec's own explicit scope note, the ~600 pre-existing dead/unreferenced keys in `i18n.ts` remain unpruned by design — pruning is a separate, more mechanical cleanup task with its own risk (a key that looks unused via static grep could still be referenced through exactly the dynamic-template pattern above) and was never part of this correctness-only sweep.

(2) same job had no test step before publishing -- FIXED with a plain `go test ./...` (49/49 passing), declined full lint/SAST tooling as scope creep (no such tooling exists anywhere else in this repo's Go CI). (3) agent.ts's browser-dev-only fallback path (never used in the shipped Tauri app) did unvalidated string concatenation of the external-agent base URL -- FIXED with a new resolveAgentBaseUrl helper (rejects non-http(s) scheme + userinfo) + 2 new tests; reviewer independently grepped all 13 agentGet/agentPost call sites confirming `path` is always a trusted literal (unlike Rust's genuinely-attacker-reachable IPC path arg), so no charset restriction needed here. (4) useAgentSupervisor's exponential backoff was a passive cooldown gate that never actually triggered a recheck -- real cadence was capped at the 20s health-poll interval regardless of backoff value -- FIXED by having the cooldown timer force queryClient.refetchQueries() instead of waiting for the next scheduled poll; reviewer EMPIRICALLY proved the fix necessary by reverting just this file to pre-fix and re-running the test (failed exactly as predicted), then confirmed TanStack's per-query fetch dedup prevents a double-network-call when this forced refetch overlaps the independently-scheduled 20s poll (confirmed useAgentHealth() genuinely has 2 simultaneous observers in production: AgentLifecycle + Run.tsx). (5) spec doc wording fixed to match actual committed-vs-local-only externalBin behavior (real inconsistency CodeRabbit caught: spec said externalBin gets written into tauri.conf.json, contradicting the plan's own binding "stays []" constraint -- a self-review gap from the spec-writing phase that never got backported after the plan-writing phase corrected it). DECLINED: markdownlint fence-language nitpick on a throwaway .superpowers/sdd/ report file (not real documentation). Non-blocking follow-ups noted by the fix-reviewer (not fixed, judged not reachable in the actual UI-constrained usage): resolveAgentBaseUrl's new(path,base) silently drops any path-segment in base_url (fine since the UI/i18n placeholder only ever collects a bare host:port origin, never a path); "resets after a healthy poll" test doesn't drive failure count to threshold first (pre-existing gap, not introduced by this fix). Merge conflict with origin/main (P5.3.3 a11y audit merged first) resolved as a trivial append-only ledger conflict (kept both blocks). Fix commit 845d8db, full suite 72/72 + typecheck + build + YAML + go test all green.
=== P5.3.4 PR #102 CI FAILURE (post-review, found by user) ===
CI's `validate / TypeScript Type Check` + `Docker Build Combined Image` both failed on push: `src/i18n-key-usage.test.ts` imports node:fs/node:path/node:url, but `web/tsconfig.app.json` (covering src/**) only listed `"types": ["vite/client"]` -- Node's ambient module declarations were never visible there, only to `tsconfig.node.json`'s narrower vite.config.ts/vitest.config.ts scope (which already had `"types": ["node"]`). ROOT CAUSE OF WHY THIS WASN'T CAUGHT EARLIER: `web/` is NOT an npm workspace member (root package.json's `workspaces` array is `["packages/*", "panel", "desktop"]` -- web has its own separate package-lock.json/node_modules). Every local gate run across Task 1, its reviewer, Task 2, and the final whole-branch review had accumulated local `web/node_modules` state (from however many `npm install`s across this session) that happened to make the missing-types bug invisible -- confirmed by reproducing locally: `mv node_modules node_modules.bak && npm ci` (a truly clean install matching CI exactly) reproduces the identical 3 TS2307 errors. Every single "web gates green" claim in this initiative's prior task/review reports was accurate against a contaminated environment, not a genuinely fresh one -- nobody's local verification was fabricated, but none of it was checking what CI actually checks. FIX (commit 53b8d1e): added `"node"` alongside `"vite/client"` in tsconfig.app.json's types array (matches tsconfig.node.json's existing pattern; @types/node was already present in web/package-lock.json as a transitive dependency, no new dependency added). Re-verified against the SAME clean npm-ci'd node_modules: typecheck/test/lint/build all pass. LESSON for future web/ work: web/'s standalone (non-workspace) lockfile means its local node_modules can silently drift from what a genuinely fresh `npm ci` produces in a way that never happens for workspace members (panel/packages-ui/desktop) whose install is unified at the root -- when in doubt about a web/ gate, verify against a truly fresh `npm ci`, not just whatever's already installed.

=== P5.3.5 FINAL WHOLE-BRANCH REVIEW (opus, 294a59f..7aaa2f3) — READY TO MERGE: YES WITH FOLLOW-UPS, 0 Critical / 0 Important (blocking) / 2 Minor (noted, no action) ===

Also confirmed the scale test cleanly SKIPS (not fails) when TEST_DATABASE_URL is unset, so contributors without a local Postgres are unaffected. Cross-task consistency verified: Task 2's forward-referencing comment (written before Task 3 existed) now accurately describes the real PGStore.AnalyzeAttendeesTable/BulkCreateAttendees at final HEAD. Minor (noted, no action): (1) the 100ms timing assertion is a single-sample measurement per shape, not best-of-N — margin is generous (100ms vs ~2-18ms observed) so flake risk is low but non-zero; if it ever flakes on a noisy CI runner, fix via best-of-N/median, not by raising the bound; (2) ANALYZE attendees runs table-wide once per 500-row bulk-import chunk (not scoped to just-inserted rows, since Postgres's ANALYZE doesn't support that) — reviewer's own research confirmed ANALYZE takes only a SHARE UPDATE EXCLUSIVE lock (doesn't block concurrent reads/writes) and is sampling-based, so no real multi-tenant contention risk, just modest redundant per-chunk work; a future cleanup could run it once at end-of-import instead. Gates (reviewer-run): full backend suite 617+/617+ (both with and without TEST_DATABASE_URL), go vet, go build, golangci-lint all clean. Scope confirmed exactly 9 files, zero migrations, zero new indexes — the "pivot to a measured fix" narrative holds up fully against the actual diff.
